The chapter's secondary forward-link is to Part II C7 (the comparative chapter on the inversion / transformation problem, ch. 40 of the present volume) — where the present chapter contributes both halves as cases at the structurally-adjacent boundary of the chaoskampf category that test the typology's application range, distinct from the inversion characterisation of the Ch28 Bida case and from the transformation characterisations of the Ch23 Susanoo and Ch26 Pariacaca cases, with the inclusion-marginal characterisation of the present chapter being its own typological-engagement category that C7 is to engage with alongside the inversion and transformation characterisations.footnote:[Per brief 30-bakunawa.yaml on the chapter's contribution to Part II C7 as cases at the structurally-adjacent boundary of the chaoskampf category; per scope.md §"Book structure" Part II C7 on the inversion / transformation problem comparative chapter (ch. 40 of the present volume); per the chapter's [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker on the distinction between the inclusion-marginal characterisation of the present chapter and the inversion characterisation of Ch28 Bida and the transformation characterisations of Ch23 Susanoo and Ch26 Pariacaca.]
// EVIDENCE: source_id=harva-altaic-religious ; loc=Die religiösen Vorstellungen der altaischen Völker, on the Erlik / Ülgen pairing in the Altaic / Turkic-Mongol cosmological scheme

The chapter's contribution to the methods sidebar (chapter 33 of the present volume, between Part I and Part II) is on three methodological points: the oral-tradition-to-text recoding situation (the Bakunawa and Erlik / Ülgen materials being 19th-20th-century folkloric-and-ethnographic-recording corpora rather than pre-modern manuscript traditions, which the chapter handles via the [LACUNA] marker on pre-modern attestations and via continuous methodological registration of the colonial-ethnographic mediation in both Spanish-and-American-colonial-Philippine and Russian-Imperial-Altaic forms); the inclusion-marginal characterisation methodological move (the use of the comparativist inclusion-marginal characterisation as a heuristic for cross-cultural reflection rather than as a tradition-internal characterisation, distinct from the inversion / transformation methodological moves of the Ch28 / Ch23 / Ch26 chapters); and the area-specialist citation policy as applied to non-Eurasian non-textual traditions (which the chapter handles via the [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] marker and via the named-but-flagged secondary-anchor pattern for Potanin, Verbitsky, and Radloff alongside the Eugenio, Eliade, and Harva anchors).footnote:[Per brief 30-bakunawa.yaml special_instructions on the area-specialist citation policy and on the colonial-ethnographic-mediation textual-witness situation common to both halves of the chapter; per scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" on the area-specialist citation requirement, and per scope.md §"Reconstruction policy" point 1 on no cross-tradition reconstruction; chapter 33 methods sidebar (per toc.yaml) as the chapter that articulates these methodological points at full length; the chapter's status as a related-tier family chapter testing the typology's application range at its outer boundaries makes it a relevant reference point for the methods sidebar's discussion of comparativist heuristics held at appropriate distance from area-specialist consensus.]
// EVIDENCE: source_id=eugenio-philippine-myths ; loc=Philippine Folk Literature: The Myths, sections on Bakunawa and the moons

The chapter's principal back-links within the present book are to chapter 28 on Bida and the founding of Wagadu (the inversion anchor, with which the present chapter shares the inclusion-marginal-cases-of-related-tier-non-Eurasian-material classification but contrasts in the substance of the inclusion-marginality — Bida is the inversion case where the chaoskampf structural features are present with valences reversed at every load-bearing point, while the present chapter's two halves are inclusion-marginal at different specific structural points), to chapter 27 on the Mapuche Kai-Kai / Tren-Tren material (related-tier non-Eurasian-cluster co-comparandum with the cosmogonic-cataclysm-and-ngillatun-ritual-foundation reading), and to chapters 6 (Illuyanka in the *purulli*-festival cyclical-maintenance context) and 16 (Ra-Apep in the daily-solar-cycle cyclical-maintenance context) as the principal Eurasian cyclical-maintenance comparanda against which the Bakunawa half's communal-prophylactic register is contrasted.footnote:[Per scope.md §"Book structure" cluster 11 (Africa), cluster 10 (Americas), and cluster 12 (Southeast Asia & Oceania) on the chapter ordering; per brief 28-bida-wagadu.yaml, brief 27-mapuche-kai-tren.yaml, and the present brief 30-bakunawa.yaml on the related-tier classifications; per scope.md §"Subject definition" combat-myth register 3 (cyclical maintenance) on the *purulli*-festival and daily-solar-cycle cyclical-maintenance contexts of chapters 6 and 16 against which the Bakunawa half's communal-prophylactic register is contrasted.]
// EVIDENCE: source_id=eugenio-philippine-myths ; loc=Philippine Folk Literature: The Myths, sections on Bakunawa and the moons

The chapter closes by registering its load-bearing methodological function for the present book as a whole: the chapter is the present book's principal worked instance of the *inclusion-marginal cases* methodological move — the registration of cases at the structurally-adjacent boundary of the chaoskampf category that test the typology's application range without inversion (Ch28 Bida) or transformation (Ch23 Susanoo, Ch26 Pariacaca) framing applying — with the chapter's two halves contributing two specific inclusion-marginality grounds (no hero-slaying / communal-prophylactic register for Bakunawa; non-serpentine adversary and non-decisive opposition / dualistic-cosmology comparandum for Erlik / Ülgen) on which the methodological move rests, and with the chapter's forward-link to Part II C8 (ch. 41 of the present volume) as a PRINCIPAL CASE for the chaoskampf-frame-applies-only-partially-at-best argument being the methodological-function load-bearing output of the chapter for the book as a whole.footnote:[Per brief 30-bakunawa.yaml special_instructions on the chapter's status as a PRINCIPAL CASE for the Part II C8 chaoskampf-frame-applies-only-partially-at-best argument and on the chapter's two halves contributing two specific inclusion-marginality grounds; per scope.md §"Book structure" Part II C8 on the refusal and the appropriation problem comparative chapter (ch. 41 of the present volume); per the chapter's load-bearing methodological function for the present book as the principal worked instance of the inclusion-marginal-cases methodological move distinct from inversion and transformation.]
// EVIDENCE: source_id=harva-altaic-religious ; loc=Die religiösen Vorstellungen der altaischen Völker, on the Erlik / Ülgen pairing in the Altaic / Turkic-Mongol cosmological scheme

// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Egypt (Ra-Apep, Ch. 16) — daily cyclical-maintenance register contrast structurally closest to the Bakunawa half's communal-prophylactic register: the daily Apep-overthrowing ritual of the Egyptian solar-cycle is the cyclical-maintenance practice in the strong sense, in which a hero-deity-led combat against the chaos-bringer is *re-enacted* daily as the means of maintaining the cosmic order; the communal-noise-making practice during eclipses against Bakunawa is structurally a *communal-prophylactic* practice in the no-hero-figure register, in which the human-community-led response to the serpent's emergence drives the serpent off without re-enacting any underlying hero-led combat (since none is recorded in the Bakunawa cycle), and the practice's communal-and-recurring character is its principal structural feature. The Apep-Bakunawa contrast is registered for Part II C8 as the principal worked instance of the inclusion-marginal-cyclical-maintenance distinction at the daily-solar-cycle level — the Bakunawa half's most precise structural comparandum within the present book.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Anatolia (Illuyanka, Ch. 6) — *purulli*-festival cyclical-maintenance contrast: the Hittite Illuyanka material's *purulli*-festival ritual context is the cyclical-maintenance register in the explicit-festival-attached form, with the Tarḫunna-versus-Illuyanka combat-narrative recited as the festival's textual centre and the festival itself maintaining the cosmic-and-political order across the annual cycle; the Bakunawa eclipse-response practice is structurally a counterpart cyclical-maintenance practice but in the no-hero-figure communal-prophylactic register rather than the hero-led-re-enactive register, and the practice's structural difference from the *purulli*-festival pattern is the load-bearing inclusion-marginal feature of the Bakunawa half. The Illuyanka-Bakunawa contrast is registered for Part II C8 as a worked instance of the inclusion-marginal-cyclical-maintenance distinction at the festival-attached level.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Iran (Thraētaona / Aži Dahāka, Ch. 13) — Indo-Iranian dualistic-cosmology comparandum for the Erlik / Ülgen half: the Avestan tradition's Ahura Mazdā / Angra Mainyu dualistic cosmology (treated within the Thraētaona / Aži Dahāka chapter alongside the Frashokereti eschatological pendant) is the principal Indo-Iranian dualistic-cosmology comparandum to the Erlik / Ülgen pairing at the structural level of the high-god-and-adversarial-counterpart pairing; the parallel is registered as an independent typological convergence rather than as a transmission relationship — the Altaic / Turkic-Mongol material is not held in current Altaic-studies and history-of-religions scholarship to inherit from the Indo-Iranian material — and the contrast at the level of the decisive-combat feature (the Indo-Iranian material develops the Frashokereti decisive-combat in the eschatological register, whereas the Altaic material does not develop a decisive-combat resolution in any register) is the load-bearing inclusion-marginal feature of the Erlik / Ülgen half within the chaoskampf typology. The Thraētaona-Erlik / Ülgen contrast is registered for Part II C8 as a worked instance of the inclusion-marginal-dualistic-cosmology comparandum.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Africa (Bida and the founding of Wagadu, Ch. 28) — non-Eurasian-cluster inclusion-marginal-versus-inversion contrast: the Ch28 Bida case is the inversion case in the strong sense (the chaoskampf structural features are present with valences reversed at every load-bearing point — the serpent is the protector of the city's prosperity, the slaying ends rather than establishes the prosperity, the cycle of ritual maintenance is broken rather than re-enacted), while the present chapter's Bakunawa half is inclusion-marginal in the no-hero-slaying sense and the Erlik / Ülgen half is inclusion-marginal in the non-serpentine-and-non-decisive sense, with the three cases between them representing three different non-Eurasian-cluster typological-engagement categories within Part II C7 / C8 — inversion (Bida), no-hero-slaying-communal-prophylactic (Bakunawa), and non-serpentine-non-decisive-dualistic-cosmology (Erlik / Ülgen) — that the comparative-engagement chapters of Part II are to engage with rather than paper over.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Mapuche Kai-Kai vs. Tren-Tren (Ch. 27) — non-Eurasian-cluster co-comparandum at the related-tier level: the Mapuche material's two-serpent cosmogonic-cataclysm-and-ngillatun-ritual-foundation reading is registered (without consultation of the Mapuche-chapter material itself per the parallel-agent task-discipline applied at the Ch27 / Ch28 stage) as a related-tier non-Eurasian comparandum at the same level of the typology as the present chapter's two halves; the contrast between the Mapuche material's transformation characterisation (cosmogonic-cataclysm-within-existing-cosmos rather than cosmos-versus-chaos combat) and the present chapter's inclusion-marginal characterisation (the Bakunawa cycle's no-hero-slaying communal-prophylactic register; the Erlik / Ülgen pairing's non-serpentine-non-decisive dualistic-cosmology comparandum) is registered for Part II C7 and C8 as a worked instance of the spectrum of typological-engagement categories at the related-tier level.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Methods sidebar (Ch. 33) — the present chapter is a worked instance of three methodological moves: (1) the appropriation-protocol's outside-framing requirement (scope.md §"Appropriation protocol" point 3) applied to two parallel oral-tradition materials in two distinct cultural-areal contexts (Philippine and Altaic / Turkic-Mongol), with the chapter opening with each tradition's own framing — Eugenio's Philippine eclipse-aetiology / communal-ritual framing for Bakunawa, Eliade's and Harva's dualistic-cosmology / shamanic-complex framing for Erlik / Ülgen — before invoking the comparative chaoskampf category; (2) the inclusion-marginal-characterisation methodological move (the use of the comparativist inclusion-marginal characterisation as a heuristic for cross-cultural reflection rather than as a tradition-internal characterisation, distinct from the inversion / transformation methodological moves of the Ch28 / Ch23 / Ch26 chapters), which the present chapter establishes for the present book and which Part II C8 (Ch. 41) develops at full length; (3) the named-but-flagged secondary-anchor pattern for non-Eurasian non-textual traditions (Potanin, Verbitsky, and Radloff named in body prose alongside the Eugenio, Eliade, and Harva anchors but not load-bearing for any individual EVIDENCE-anchored claim), per the Ch23 FC-02 / Ch26 FC-02 / Ch27 / Ch28 named-but-flagged precedent.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Part II C7 (the inversion / transformation problem, Ch. 40) — the present chapter is a working example of cases at the structurally-adjacent boundary of the chaoskampf category that test the typology's application range without inversion (Ch28 Bida) or transformation (Ch23 Susanoo, Ch26 Pariacaca) framing applying; the inclusion-marginal characterisation of the present chapter is its own typological-engagement category that C7 is to engage with alongside the inversion and transformation characterisations, with the two halves of the chapter contributing two specific inclusion-marginality grounds (no hero-slaying / communal-prophylactic register for Bakunawa; non-serpentine adversary and non-decisive opposition / dualistic-cosmology comparandum for Erlik / Ülgen) on which the methodological-engagement work of C7 rests for the present chapter's contribution.
// COMPARATIVE-HOOK: Part II C8 (the refusal and the appropriation problem, Ch. 41) — PRIMARY FORWARD TARGET. The present chapter is a PRINCIPAL CASE for the chaoskampf-frame-applies-only-partially-at-best argument per brief 30-bakunawa.yaml special_instructions, contributing both the Bakunawa half (no-hero-slaying / communal-prophylactic register; area-specialist objection-strength closer to the Ch32 Nanabozho refusal case than to the milder Ch26 Pariacaca and Ch27 Mapuche cases) and the Erlik / Ülgen half (non-serpentine-and-non-decisive / dualistic-cosmology comparandum; structurally distinctive strong-objection case in which the dualistic-cosmology framing and the chaoskampf typology converge on no structural feature at the load-bearing level) as PRINCIPAL CASES for the C8 argument. The chapter's load-bearing methodological move — using the inclusion-marginal characterisation as a heuristic for cross-cultural reflection rather than as a tradition-internal characterisation — is the move that C8 is to engage with directly at full length, alongside the parallel methodological moves of the Ch23 Susanoo / Yamata no Orochi material, the Ch26 Pariacaca cycle, the Ch27 Mapuche Kai-Kai / Tren-Tren material, the Ch28 Bida / Wagadu material, the Ch29 Mwindo / Kirimu material, the Ch32 Nanabozho / Mishipeshu material, and the Rainbow Serpent material (folded into C8 per toc.yaml self_checks).

    triangulations_assumed: >
      (1) BAKUNAWA SEVEN-MOONS NARRATIVE: The narrative premise that seven original moons
      existed of which six were devoured by Bakunawa is correctly identified as the
      "most widely attested form" per Eugenio 2001. Per trained knowledge: the seven-moons
      version is the dominant recorded form in the Visayan/Bikol corpus. PASS.
      (2) ECLIPSE-AS-DEVOURING: The eclipse interpreted within the tradition as Bakunawa's
      devouring action upon the last moon is correctly characterised per Eugenio. PASS.
      (3) COMMUNAL NOISE-MAKING PRACTICES: Drums, gongs, shouting, banging metal pots —
      these are correctly described as the eclipse-response practices in the recorded
      Bakunawa cycle. PASS.
      (4) BAKUNAWA DWELLING: Deep sea in dominant Visayan recording; underworld in some
      recordings — both are correctly registered as variant attestations. PASS.
      (5) VISAYAN AND BIKOL AS HEARTLANDS: Correct per trained knowledge of Philippine
      ethnographic geography; the Visayan island group and the Bikol region of southeastern
      Luzon are the principal attestation zones for the Bakunawa cycle. PASS.
      (6) PHILIPPINE COLONIAL PERIODS: Spanish colonial (1565–1898) and American colonial

      is canonical in the scholarly literature. PASS.
      (8) ERLIK AS ANTHROPOMORPHIC UNDERWORLD-RULER: Non-serpentine characterisation is
      correct per Harva 1938; Erlik is consistently described in the recorded versions
      as anthropomorphic (human-like) rather than serpentine, in contrast to the Eurasian
      chaoskampf adversaries. PASS.
      (9) WHITE-SHAMAN / BLACK-SHAMAN DIVISION: Correctly attributed to Eliade 1964;
      the division of Altaic shamanic specialisation into sky-directed (Ülgen) and
      underworld-directed (Erlik) strands is a standard feature of the Altaic-Siberian
      shamanic complex literature. PASS.
      (10) ERLIK AS FALLEN-FROM-ÜLGEN IN SOME VARIANTS: Some recordings present Erlik
      as a fallen or expelled figure from Ülgen's realm; others present the two as
      co-eternal independent powers. Both are correctly registered as legitimate variant
      attestations. PASS.
      (11) POTANIN, VERBITSKY, RADLOFF AS FOUNDATIONAL ETHNOGRAPHERS: Named correctly;
      all three are canonical figures in the 19th-century Russian/European ethnographic
      recording corpus for Altaic/Turkic-Mongol peoples. None is in sources.yaml.
      Named-but-flagged pattern is correctly applied — none carries an EVIDENCE token.
      NOT LOAD-BEARING for any individual claim. PASS.
      (12) AHURA MAZDĀ / ANGRA MAINYU AS PARALLEL: The claim that the Erlik/Ülgen pairing
      parallels the Avestan Ahura Mazdā/Angra Mainyu dualistic cosmology as an independent
      typological convergence rather than a transmission relationship is the correct
      framing in current Altaic-studies and history-of-religions scholarship. Per trained
      knowledge of the field: (a) there is no established genetic/transmission link between
      Altaic and Avestan dualisms in current scholarship; (b) the parallel is noted as a
      structural-typological convergence in comparative-religion literature (including
      Eliade); (c) the claim that this is NOT held to be a transmission relationship in
      current Altaic-studies scholarship is accurate — the two dualisms are independently
      attested in geographically adjacent but culturally distinct traditions. The chapter's
      framing ("independent typological convergence rather than transmission relationship")
      is the standard and defensible scholarly position. PASS — Ahura Mazdā/Angra Mainyu
      independent-convergence framing judgment: CONFIRMED as current consensus.
      (13) POTANIN, VERBITSKY, RADLOFF NOT LOAD-BEARING: Correct. All three are named
      in body prose in the Source overview §Erlik/Ülgen recording-corpus claim with
      explicit flagging that "none is currently a sources.yaml entry." None appears in
      any EVIDENCE token. Named-but-flagged pattern correctly applied per Ch23 FC-02 /
      Ch26 FC-02 / Ch27 / Ch28 FC-02 precedent. PASS.
      (14) BAKUNAWA CYCLE: NO PRE-MODERN WRITTEN ATTESTATION: Correctly characterised;
      per trained knowledge of Philippine indigenous-script traditions (Baybayin): there
      is no known pre-Hispanic-contact written attestation of the Bakunawa cycle in
      Baybayin or any other Philippine indigenous script. The claim that no pre-modern
      attestation is available is factually accurate. PASS.
      (15) ERLIK/ÜLGEN: NO PRE-MODERN WRITTEN RECORD: Correctly characterised; per
      trained knowledge: the principal written attestations of Erlik/Ülgen cosmology are
      all 19th-20th-century. The qualified note that "passing references in the writings
      of medieval Islamic geographers and travellers" exist is appropriately cautious.
      PASS.
      (16) BAKUNAWA CYCLE'S FUNCTION: ECLIPSE-AETIOLOGY NOT COSMOGONY: Correctly
      characterised as the cycle's primary cultural-historical function. The cycle explains
      eclipses (recurring observable phenomenon) rather than original cosmogonic creation.
      This distinction is correct and important for the inclusion-marginal characterisation.
      PASS.
      (17) STRUCTURAL ABSENCE OF HERO-FIGURE: The characterisation that the Bakunawa
      cycle has no individual hero (deity, champion, or human protagonist) who confronts
      and defeats the serpent is correct per trained knowledge of the cycle's recorded
      versions; communal noise-making is the response in all principal recordings. PASS.

# AHURA MAZDA / ANGRA MAINYU INDEPENDENT-CONVERGENCE FRAMING
# ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

ahura_mazda_angra_mainyu_framing:
  claim_location: "§Erlik and Ülgen: dualistic cosmology and inclusion-marginal status, line 133"
  claim_text: >
    The Erlik/Ülgen pairing parallels the Indo-Iranian Ahura Mazdā/Angra Mainyu
    dualistic cosmology at the structural level of the high-god-and-adversarial-counterpart
    pairing, but does not inherit from the Indo-Iranian material. The structural parallel
    is registered as an independent typological convergence.
  judgment: CONFIRMED_CORRECT
  reasoning: >
    Per trained knowledge of current Altaic-studies and history-of-religions scholarship:
    (1) There is no established genetic or transmission link between the Altaic/Turkic-Mongol
    dualism (Erlik/Ülgen) and the Avestan dualism (Ahura Mazdā/Angra Mainyu) in current
    scholarship. Proposals of Iranian religious influence on Altaic religions exist in
    the older comparative-religion literature but are not the current consensus.
    (2) The structural parallel at the level of the high-god / adversarial-counterpart
    pairing is real and noted in comparative-religion literature including Eliade.
    (3) The formulation "independent typological convergence rather than transmission
    relationship" is the standard and defensible scholarly position for a cross-cultural
    structural parallel without demonstrated transmission.
    (4) The chapter correctly cross-references Ch13 (Thraētaona / Aži Dahāka) where the
    Ahura Mazdā / Angra Mainyu dualism is treated within the Indo-Iranian context.
    (5) The contrast at the level of the decisive-combat feature (Frashokereti eschatological
    combat in the Avestan tradition vs. non-decisive arrangement in the Altaic tradition)
    is correctly registered as the load-bearing inclusion-marginal feature.
    The Ahura Mazdā / Angra Mainyu independent-convergence framing is CONFIRMED as
    consistent with current Altaic-studies and history-of-religions consensus. PASS.
  sources_used: "Harva 1938, Eliade 1964 (via trained knowledge of each volume)"

findings:

  - id: FC-01
    severity: LOW
    category: identifier_mismatch
    location: >
      sources.yaml — eugenio-philippine-myths entry, identifier_value field.
    claim_text: >
      sources.yaml pins identifier_value: "9789715421140" for Eugenio 2001,
      *Philippine Folk Literature: The Myths* (UP Press).
    problem: >
      The pinned ISBN-13 (9789715421140) is incorrect. The confirmed correct ISBN-13,
      per the UP Press product page (https://press.up.edu.ph/product/philippine-folk-literature-the-myths/),
      AbeBooks listing (9789715422918), and multiple bibliographic sources, is 9789715422918.
      The two ISBNs differ at the final digits (−1140 vs. −2918). The content of the volume
      and its series placement are correctly described in sources.yaml; only the identifier
      is wrong. Sources.yaml's own notes field flags this as "provisional pending factcheck
      verification" — the flag is correctly set and the factcheck now supplies the
      correction.
    evidence: >
      UP Press product page for *Philippine Folk Literature: The Myths* returns
      ISBN 978971542291-8; AbeBooks listing explicitly cites 9789715422918 for Vol. 2
      of the Philippine Folk Literature series. Both independent sources agree.
    recommended_fix: >
      At post-human-normalize: correct identifier_value in sources.yaml from "9789715421140"
      to "9789715422918" per the Ch20 FC-03 / Ch24 FC-03 ISBN-correction-in-place pattern.
      Update the notes field to remove the provisional flag and record the correction date.
      No change to any claims file: the identifier mismatch is in sources.yaml only; no
      EVIDENCE token in the claims file cites the ISBN directly. LOW-priority — all
      content claims anchored to eugenio-philippine-myths are substantively correct.

  - id: FC-02
    severity: LOW
    category: identifier_mismatch
    location: >
      sources.yaml — harva-altaic-religious entry, identifier_value field.
    claim_text: >
      sources.yaml pins identifier_value:
      "https://archive.org/details/diereligiosenvor0000unkn" for Harva 1938,
      *Die religiösen Vorstellungen der altaischen Völker*, FFC 125.
    problem: >
      The pinned stable-url identifier does not correspond to the correct archive.org
      record for this work. The confirmed archive.org URL, per direct web search, is
      https://archive.org/details/DieReligioenVorstellungenDerAltaischenVolker
      (identifier: "DieReligioenVorstellungenDerAltaischenVolker"). The pinned identifier
      "diereligiosenvor0000unkn" appears to be a placeholder or an incorrect OCLC-pattern
      identifier rather than the actual archive.org stable-url. Sources.yaml's own notes
      field flags this as "provisional pending factcheck verification" and recommends
      checking the OCLC catalogue at normalize — the flag is correctly set and the
      factcheck now supplies the archive.org correction.
      NOTE: The archive.org record lists the author as "Uno Holmberg" (Harva's birth name,
      before his 1935 name change). Sources.yaml correctly cites "Harva, Uno" — no
      correction needed there.
    evidence: >
      Web search confirms archive.org identifier is "DieReligioenVorstellungenDerAltaischenVolker"
      at https://archive.org/details/DieReligioenVorstellungenDerAltaischenVolker. The
      search did not return any record matching the pinned identifier "diereligiosenvor0000unkn."
    recommended_fix: >
      At post-human-normalize: correct identifier_value in sources.yaml from
      "https://archive.org/details/diereligiosenvor0000unkn" to
      "https://archive.org/details/DieReligioenVorstellungenDerAltaischenVolker". Also
      check OCLC WorldCat for the FFC 125 OCLC number as a more institutionally stable
      identifier (OCLC is more stable than archive.org over multi-year horizons). Update
      the notes field to remove the provisional flag and record the correction date.
      No change to any claims file: the identifier mismatch is in sources.yaml only.
      LOW-priority — all content claims anchored to harva-altaic-religious are
      substantively correct; the stable-url fix is a bibliographic housekeeping item.

# Input file: briefs/29-mwindo-kirimu.yaml

```
chapter_number: 29
slug: "mwindo-kirimu"
title: "Mwindo and Kirimu (The Contrastive Case)"
chapter_anchor: "ch-29-mwindo-kirimu"

chapter_type: "contrastive (full)"

sources:
  primary:
    - id: biebuyck-mateene-mwindo
      loc: "The Mwindo Epic, episode of Kirimu"
      identifier: "ISBN 9780520003767"
    - id: belcher-epic
      loc: "Epic Traditions of Africa, ch. on Mwindo"
      identifier: "ISBN 9780253212818"
  secondary: []

variants:
  classification: single-prevalent
  summary: |
    The Biebuyck & Mateene 1969 text (Shé-Kárisi Rureke's performance) is the standard
    primary text. Biebuyck later published additional Nyanga epics with related material.
    The chapter uses Biebuyck & Mateene 1969 as the anchor.

summary: |
  In the Nyanga Mwindo epic, the hero kills the monstrous dragon Kirimu — and is then
  punished by the sky-god Nkuba for the killing. The moral valence is inverted from
  chaoskampf: the dragon-slaying is hubris, not order-making. The hero must undergo
  humiliation and re-integration.

cultural_relevance:
  centrality: |
    Central within Nyanga oral-epic tradition (one of the flagship African oral epics in
    20th-century scholarship); significant as type-case in African epic studies.
  function: |
    - Didactic (the hero's maturation through humiliation)
    - Social-moral (reciprocal balance between the human and spirit worlds)
    - Religious-political (the sky-god's authority over the hero)
  cross_cultural_parallels: |
    - Bida (Chapter 28) and Mwindo together make the African material the book's strongest
      "the pattern doesn't go where comparativists expect" cluster.
    - Mwindo's punishment-for-killing structurally echoes Krishna subduing-not-killing
      Kāliya (Chapter 15) — though the Krishna case is a moral transformation within the
      same tradition (Indra-as-precursor), whereas Mwindo is a different tradition entirely.

target_length_words: 5000

special_instructions: |
  CONTRASTIVE case per scope.md §"In-scope catalog" — treat as a full-length chapter that
  shows what a very thorough combat-myth looks like when its moral frame refuses chaoskampf.
  The chapter's role is load-bearing: it is the clearest case in the book of a tradition
  whose own framing explicitly rejects the chaos-order mapping. Area-specialist citation
  policy applies: cite Biebuyck and Mateene by name throughout; acknowledge the oral-
  performance context (Shé-Kárisi Rureke was the narrator in 1956). The chapter feeds
  Part II C7 (inversion) and especially C8 (refusal and appropriation). The chapter must
  not be apologetic about the Mwindo material's resistance to the chaoskampf frame —
  the resistance is the data.
```

# Input file: briefs/30-bakunawa.yaml

```
chapter_number: 30
slug: "bakunawa"
title: "Bakunawa and the Moons (with Erlik/Ülgen as Altaic Comparandum)"
chapter_anchor: "ch-30-bakunawa"

chapter_type: "family (related-tier, 'communal / non-slaying combat')"

sources:
  primary:
    - id: eugenio-philippine-myths
      loc: "Philippine Folk Literature: The Myths, sections on Bakunawa and the moons"
      identifier: "ISBN 9789715421140"
  secondary:
    - id: eliade-shamanism
      loc: "Shamanism: Archaic Techniques of Ecstasy, on the Erlik / Ülgen dualistic cosmology and Altaic-Siberian shamanic complex"
      identifier: "ISBN 9780691119427"
    - id: harva-altaic-religious
      loc: "Die religiösen Vorstellungen der altaischen Völker, on the Erlik / Ülgen pairing in the Altaic / Turkic-Mongol cosmological scheme"
      identifier: "stable-url: https://archive.org/details/diereligiosenvor0000unkn"
    - id: forsyth-1987
      loc: "combat-myth long-arc typology (Sumer through Judeo-Christian apocalyptic); not for Philippine or Altaic-specific coverage"
      identifier: "ISBN 9780691014746"

source_anchoring_notes: |
  Three anchors were pinned in sources.yaml at the start of this chapter-claims cycle
  (commit pending), resolving the inventory.approved.yaml identifier_missing flag for
  the bakunawa and erlik-ulgen entries. Eugenio 2001 (Philippine Folk Literature: The
  Myths) is the principal anchor for the Bakunawa material; Eliade 1964 (Shamanism)
  and Harva 1938 (Die religiösen Vorstellungen der altaischen Völker, FFC 125) are the
  principal anchors for the Erlik / Ülgen material. Primary ethnographic sources for
  Erlik / Ülgen (Potanin, Verbitsky, Radloff) are not pinned and may be added at chapter-
  draft if a specific narrative detail genuinely requires direct citation; otherwise the
  named-but-flagged pattern (Ch23 FC-02 / Ch26 FC-02 / Ch27 / Ch28 precedent) applies
  for any scholar named in body prose without a sources.yaml entry. Identifier values
  are provisional pending factcheck verification per the Ch27 source-pinning precedent
  (the Ch20 FC-03 / Ch24 FC-03 ISBN-correction-in-place pattern at post-human-normalize).

family_members:
  - name: "Bakunawa and the moons (Visayan / Bikol)"
    summary: "The serpent-dragon Bakunawa devours six of the seven original moons; to save the last, communities make ritual noise (drums, gongs, shouting) to drive the serpent off during eclipses. There is no hero who slays it — the combat is communal and recurring. Eclipse-aetiology, not hero-slaying."
  - name: "Erlik vs. Ülgen (Altaic / Turkic-Mongol)"
    summary: "In Altaic and broader Turkic-Mongol mythology, the sky-god Ülgen opposes the underworld-god Erlik; the opposition is dualistic and cosmogonic rather than straightforwardly combat-resolved. Per audit-review-log.md 2026-04-23: INCLUSION-MARGINAL — the adversary (Erlik) is not serpentine, and the opposition is dualistic rather than a single decisive combat. Framed as a dualistic-cosmology comparandum rather than a chaoskampf proper."

shared_variant_handling: |
  Both stories are oral-tradition material with heavy regional variability (Bakunawa across
  Philippine regional traditions; Erlik/Ülgen across Altai, Buryat, Yakut recordings).
  Edition-pinning is deferred to glossary-lock per inventory notes.

chapter_rationale_for_pairing: |
  Per toc.yaml deviation note: Erlik/Ülgen is paired with Bakunawa under the "communal /
  non-slaying combat" theme rather than placed in the IE-reflexes chapter (19). Neither
  story features a hero-slaying-monster; neither does clear cosmogonic or sovereignty work.
  Pairing them lets 30-bakunawa carry the broader "non-slaying combat" theme, and preserves
  the IE-reflexes chapter's coherence.

cultural_relevance:
  centrality: |
    Bakunawa — central in Visayan / Bikol tradition; significant as a widespread Philippine
    motif with ritual correlates.
    Erlik/Ülgen — central in Altaic / Turkic-Mongol cosmology; significant in the history
    of religions scholarship (Eliade, Harva).
  function: |
    Bakunawa: eclipse-aetiology; communal-ritual.
    Erlik/Ülgen: dualistic cosmology; underworld-sky moral structure.
  cross_cultural_parallels: |
    - Bakunawa's communal-noise-drives-serpent pattern has parallels across eclipse
      traditions (Chinese tiangou "celestial dog"); the motif may be areal.
    - Erlik/Ülgen parallels other dualistic cosmogonies (Ahura Mazdā / Angra Mainyu,
      Chapter 13), though the Altaic version lacks the decisive combat.

target_length_words: 4000

special_instructions: |
  Short family chapter (~4,000 narrative words). The three anchors above are now pinned
  (sources.yaml commit pending), so the chapter can proceed with proper EVIDENCE tokens
  routed through Eugenio 2001 (Bakunawa principal anchor) and Eliade 1964 / Harva 1938
  (Erlik / Ülgen principal anchors). CRITICAL: both stories are INCLUSION-MARGINAL for
  different reasons (no hero-slaying in Bakunawa; non-serpentine adversary and non-
  decisive opposition in Erlik/Ülgen). The chapter must be explicit about why both are
  included and in what respect they extend the book's category. Area-specialist citation
  policy applies: cite Eugenio, Eliade, and Harva by name. The chapter feeds Part II C8
  (the refusal and appropriation problem) as cases where the chaoskampf frame applies
  only partially at best.

  Strong [APPROPRIATION-FLAG:] candidate per the Ch27 / Ch28 templates: both halves of
  this chapter are inclusion-marginal precisely because area-specialists frame them
  outside the chaos-vs-order combat register (Eugenio's eclipse-aetiology / communal-
  ritual framing for Bakunawa; Eliade's and Harva's dualistic-cosmology / shamanic-
  complex framing for Erlik / Ülgen). Register named area specialists, the substance
  of the inclusion-marginal objections (no-hero-slaying for Bakunawa; non-serpentine-
  adversary and non-decisive-opposition for Erlik / Ülgen), the tier-implication
  clause, and the Ch40/Ch41 forwarding clause. The Erlik / Ülgen half should also
  cross-reference Ch13 (Thraētaona / Aži Dahāka) for the broader Indo-Iranian
  dualistic-cosmology comparandum that the Altaic material parallels but does not
  inherit from.

  Two-component chapter structure: (1) Bakunawa source-overview-and-narrative material;
  (2) Erlik / Ülgen source-overview-and-narrative material; (3) typology and forward-
  links section consolidating both halves. Use [VARIANT] markers to register the heavy
  regional variability in both halves (Bakunawa across Visayan / Bikol / other
  Philippine traditions; Erlik / Ülgen across Altai, Buryat, Yakut recordings). Use a
  [LACUNA] marker to register the oral-tradition / 19th-c.-ethnographic-recording
  filtering caveat for both halves.
```
